## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / mass-action ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard object modeled in chemical kinetics via rate laws and ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, plausible structures include mass-action polynomial rates in A, approach-to-equilibrium forms, and explicit time-dependent rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production when reactant is saturating or controlled)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition surrogate)
- Second-order (single-species) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or effective second-order loss)
- General n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order)
- Source + first-order sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (chemostat/feed term plus linear decay)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible-like net rate (quadratic equilibrium surrogate): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A - c2 * A**2 (net of forward/backward contributions reduced to A-only polynomial)
- Autocatalytic growth with depletion (logistic-form rate law): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplifying production limited by capacity/precursor depletion)
- Cubic mass-action truncation: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (effective kinetics from eliminating unobserved intermediates)
- Time-varying first-order rate (exponentially drifting k): dA_dt = -(c0 * exp(c1 * t)) * A (temperature/programmed-rate drift without explicit T)
- Periodic forcing of rate (e.g., illumination cycling): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-modulated first-order loss)
- Competing pathways (two-term loss): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular removal)
- Rational inhibition-like effective rate (A-only): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (self-inhibition or limited-availability effect expressed as an effective law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action reduction with missing species often yields low-order polynomials in A for dA_dt (linear/quadratic/cubic terms).
- Net reversible behavior with unobserved products frequently appears as relaxation toward a nonzero equilibrium: dependence on (A - A_eq).
- If A must remain nonnegative, physically plausible laws often have dA_dt ≤ 0 when A is large (dominant negative high-power terms).
- Autocatalysis tends to introduce a factor A multiplying another term, producing slow start at low A and faster change at intermediate A.
- Competing mechanisms are commonly additive in the rate: sums of separate pathway terms (e.g., -k1*A - k2*A^2).
- External experimental protocols (flow, illumination, temperature ramps) can be represented by explicit time dependence in an effective rate coefficient k(t).
- Near steady state, many kinetic systems linearize to dA_dt ≈ -c*(A - A_eq), even if the underlying mechanism is nonlinear.
- Eliminating fast intermediates (quasi-steady-state) can introduce rational forms in A (numerator/denominator polynomials) as effective kinetics.

### 1
Has extra \(A\) term, \(\sqrt{A^2+c5}\exp(c6 t)\), and \(\cos(c8 e^{c9 t})\). Can zero some, but still lacks a clean \(A e^{kt}\) term unless forcing the sqrt term to become \(A e^{kt}\) (needs \(c5=0\Rightarrow \sqrt{A^2}=|A|\), then \(A\ge0\Rightarrow |A|=A\)). But then still must also produce \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\) simultaneously: possible via \(A^2 c0\) and \(A^{c2}c3\) with \(c2=1/3\). Also must remove the plain \(A\) term by setting \(c1=0\). Remove cosine by \(c7=0\). This actually can match GT by:
- \(c0=-0.3115334933\)
- \(c1=0\)
- \(c2=1/3,\; c3=0.2331857324\)
- \(c4=-0.3115334933,\; c5=0,\; c6=-0.08476196603\)
- \(c7=0\) (kills cosine term)
Domain condition: \(A\ge 0\) so \(\sqrt{A^2}=A\).
✅ **Candidate 1 matches**.

(For completeness, I’ll still check others, but one match is enough.)

### 2
Only has \(e^{(\cdot)t}\) multiplying powers of \(|A|\), including \(|A|^{c2}\), \(|A|^2\), \(|A|\), plus pure exponentials. GT needs \(A^2\) with **no** \(t\)-dependence, and \(A^{1/3}\) with **no** \(t\)-dependence, and \(A e^{kt}\). You could set some exponents to 0 to remove \(t\)-dependence, but then you still have extra pure exponential terms unless coefficients 0. It *can* be made to match by:
- set \(c1=0\) so first term is \(c0|A|^{c2}\) with \(c2=1/3\)
- set \(c4=0\) so second/third become constants in \(t\): \(c3|A|^2 + c5|A|\)
- need \(A e^{kt}\): but remaining terms are \(c6 e^{c7 t}+c8 e^{c7 t}|A|\). If set \(c8=-0.3115\) and \(c7=-0.08476\), then \(c8 e^{c7 t}|A|\) gives the desired \(A e^{kt}\) (with \(A\ge0\)). Then must kill \(c6 e^{c7 t}\) by \(c6=0\). Also must kill unwanted \(|A|\) term by \(c5=0\). Choose \(c3=-0.3115\), \(c0=0.2331857\).
So actually ✅ matches under \(A\ge0\).  

### 3
Contains \(A^{1/3}c0\cos(Ac1)\): to match a pure \(A^{1/3}\) term, must have \(\cos(Ac1)\equiv 1\) for all \(A\), which requires \(c1=0\). Then it becomes \(c0 A^{1/3}\). Also has \(A^2 c2\). The exponential term is \(\sqrt{A^2+c4}e^{c5 t}\): set \(c4=0\) and domain \(A\ge0\) to get \(A e^{c5 t}\). Set constant \(c6=0\). Then match coefficients and \(c5=-0.08476\). ✅ matches.

### 4
Has \(A^2\), two separate linear-in-\(A\) terms, \(A^{c3}\), constant, and \(\sqrt{A^2+c7}e^{c8 t}\). Can set both linear \(A\) coefficients to 0 except we actually need an \(A e^{kt}\) term, which can come from the sqrt-exponential by setting \(c7=0\) and \(A\ge0\). Set constant \(c5=0\). Set \(c3=1/3\). ✅ matches.

### 5
Similar to 4 but uses \(c3|A|^{c4}\) for the fractional power. Set linear \(A\) terms to 0, set \(c4=1/3\), use sqrt-exp for \(A e^{kt}\) with \(c7=0\), \(A\ge0\). ✅ matches.

### 6
Like 1 but without cosine. Same construction as candidate 1 (set \(c1=0\), \(c2=1/3\), \(c5=0\), \(A\ge0\), \(c7=0\)). ✅ matches.

### 7
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), sqrt-exp, constant, and \(|A|^{c7}\). Set \(A\) term \(c1=0\), constant \(c5=0\). Use \(|A|^{c7}\) with \(c7=1/3\) for the \(A^{1/3}\) term. Use sqrt-exp with \(c3=0\), \(A\ge0\) for \(A e^{kt}\). ✅ matches.

### 8
Has \(A^2\), multiple \(A\) terms including \(A e^{c3 t}\), \(A^{c5}\), constant, and pure exponential. Can set unwanted \(A\) terms and pure exponential to 0, set \(c5=1/3\) for \(A^{1/3}\), and use \(A c2 e^{c3 t}\) for the \(A e^{kt}\) term. ✅ matches.

### 9
Has \(A^2\), sqrt-exp, constant, and \(e^{c6|A|^{1/3}}\) which is not a power term. Only way to remove that is \(c5=0\). Then no \(A^{1/3}\) term remains. ❌ no match.

### 10
Has \(c0 e^{c1 t}|A|^{c2}\) plus \(|A|^2\), \(|A|\), and \(e^{c6 t}\) terms. To get \(A^{1/3}\) without \(t\), set \(c1=0\), \(c2=1/3\). To get \(A e^{kt}\), use \(c7 e^{c6 t}|A|\) with \(c6=-0.08476\). Kill pure exponential \(c5 e^{c6 t}\) by \(c5=0\). Kill unwanted \(|A|\) by \(c4=0\). Set \(c3=-0.3115\), \(c0=0.2331857\), \(c7=-0.3115\). With \(A\ge0\), ✅ matches.

### 11
Similar flexibility: can set \(c0\) term to \(A^{1/3}\) with \(c1=0,c2=1/3\); set \(c4\) term off or use it as \(A^2\) (set \(c5=2\)); use \(c8 e^{c7 t}|A|\) for \(A e^{kt}\) with \(c7=-0.08476\); kill pure exponential \(c6 e^{c7 t}\) by \(c6=0\); kill extra \(|A|\) term by \(c3=0\). ✅ matches.

### 12
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), sqrt-exp, constant, and \(e^{c7 t}|A|^{c8}\). You can realize \(A e^{kt}\) via the last term by setting \(c8=1\), and realize \(A^{1/3}\) by setting \(c2=0\)?? No, \(c2\) is coefficient of sqrt-exp, not a power. The only fractional power available is in the last term, but that term has \(t\)-dependence. If set \(c7=0\), it becomes a pure power \(|A|^{c8}\) (good for \(1/3\)), but then you lose \(A e^{kt}\) unless sqrt-exp provides it; sqrt-exp can provide \(A e^{kt}\) by \(c3=0\), \(A\ge0\). Then set \(c7=0\) and \(c8=1/3\) for the fractional term. Set \(A\) term \(c1=0\), constant \(c5=0\). ✅ matches.

### 13
Contains \(+c8\sqrt{A^2}=c8|A|\) extra linear term unless \(c8=0\). Then it reduces to form like 8 and can match. ✅ matches.

### 14
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), \(A e^{c3 t}\), \(|A|^{c5}\), constant. Set \(c1=0\), choose \(c2=-0.3115,c3=-0.08476\), choose \(c4=0.2331857,c5=1/3\), set constant \(c6=0\). ✅ matches (with \(A\ge0\) for Abs).

### 15
Same as 14 but without Abs; can set \(c4=1/3\) directly. ✅ matches.

### 16
Like 1 but with \(|A|^{c3}\) and cosine term. Set cosine coefficient \(c7=0\). Use \(|A|^{c3}\) with \(c3=1/3\) for fractional term, use \(A^2 c0\) for quadratic, use sqrt-exp with \(c5=0\), \(A\ge0\) for \(A e^{kt}\), set linear \(A\) term \(c1=0\). ✅ matches.

### 17
Only exponentials and \(|A|^{c8}\) with exponential. Can set some exponents to 0 to make power terms; can use \(c6 e^{c7 t}|A|^{c8}\) with \(c8=1\) for \(A e^{kt}\); use \(c0 e^{c1 t}|A|^{c2}\) with \(c1=0,c2=1/3\) for fractional; but needs \(A^2\) term—none unless set \(c2=2\) which conflicts. No separate \(A^2\) power term. ❌ no match.

### 18
Has rational term \(A*c2/(A+c3)\) and \(\sqrt{A^2+c9}\) term; these can’t become pure monomials for all \(A\) except by zeroing coefficients. If zeroed, remaining terms don’t provide \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A e^{kt}\) simultaneously. ❌ no match.

### 19
Similar issue with rational terms \(A*c2/(A+c3)\) and \(c6/(A*c7+c3)\). Cannot equal GT globally unless those coefficients are 0; then lacks needed terms. ❌ no match.

### 20
\(A^2 c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2\sqrt{A^2+c3}e^{c4 t}\). Set \(c3=0\), \(A\ge0\) so sqrt gives \(A\). Then match coefficients and \(c4=-0.08476\). ✅ matches.

### 21
Same as 20 but fractional term is \(A^{1/3}c4\) absent; actually it has no explicit \(A^{1/3}\) unless via nothing—wait: it is \(A^{1/3}*c0\) yes. Then same: set \(c3=0\), \(A\ge0\). ✅ matches.

### 22
\(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c2|A|^2 + c3|A|^{1/3}\). This matches exactly the three required structures (no extra terms). Set \(c2=-0.3115\), \(c3=0.2331857\), \(c0=-0.3115\), \(c1=-0.08476\), and \(A\ge0\). ✅ matches.

### 23
\(A^2 c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2 e^{c3 t}|A|\). Exactly matches with \(A\ge0\). ✅ matches.

### 24
Same as 23 but \(A^2\) is \(|A|^2\); with \(A\ge0\) it’s fine. ✅ matches.

### 25
Contains a saturating rational term \(|A|^{c4}/(c5+|A|^{c4})\) and sqrt-exp. Rational term can be killed by setting \(c3=0\). Then it reduces to a form like 4/5 and can match. ✅ matches.

### 26
Has \(A^{c0}c1\) (power), plus \(e^{c3 t}|A|^{c4}\), plus pure exponentials. Can set pure exponential terms to 0, set \(A^{c0}\) to \(A^2\) (c0=2) and use the exp*|A| term for \(A e^{kt}\) (c4=1), but then no remaining term for \(A^{1/3}\). ❌ no match.

### 27
Has extra \(e^{A c6}\) and sqrt term; can kill them by setting coefficients \(c5=0\), \(c8=0\). Then reduces to 8-like and can match. ✅ matches.

### 28
Same as 21 plus constant; set constant \(c5=0\). ✅ matches.

### 29
Has \(A^2\), sqrt-exp, constant, and \(|A|^{1/3}\). Set constant \(c4=0\), set sqrt to \(A e^{kt}\) via \(c2=0\)?? Actually sqrt-exp coefficient is \(c1\) and inside shift \(c2\): set inside shift \(c2=0\) and \(A\ge0\). Then match. ✅ matches.

### 30
Has \(A^2\), constant, \(|A|^{1/3}\), sqrt-exp. Set constant \(c1=0\), set sqrt shift \(c4=0\), \(A\ge0\). ✅ matches.

### 31
Has \(A^2\), \(A e^{c2 t}\), \(|A|^{1/3}\), constant. Set constant \(c4=0\). Choose coefficients/exponent. ✅ matches.

### 32
Has \(A^2\), \(A e^{c2 t}\), constant, and \(|A|^{1/3}\). Set constant \(c3=0\). ✅ matches.

### 33
Has \(A^{1/3}\), \(A^2\), \(A e^{c3 t}\), constant. Set constant \(c4=0\). ✅ matches.

### 34
Only terms of form \(A e^{c1 t}\), \(e^{c3 t}|A|^{c4}\), \(e^{c6 t}|A|^{c7}\). No plain \(A^2\) term without \(t\)-dependence unless set exponent to 0, but then still not a pure polynomial term unless also remove exponentials; cannot get both \(A^2\) and \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A e^{kt}\) cleanly. ❌ no match.

### 35
Has rational terms \(A*c2/(A*c3+c4)\) and \(c8/(A+c4)\) plus sqrt-exp. Those rational terms must be zeroed (set \(c2=0,c8=0\)), then it reduces to 4-like and can match (use \(A^{c?}\) term? actually none; only \(A^2\), \(A\), sqrt-exp, constant). No \(A^{1/3}\) term remains. ❌ no match.

### 36
Similar to 35: after zeroing rational terms, still no \(A^{1/3}\). ❌ no match.

### 37
Even worse: no \(A^{1/3}\) term. ❌ no match.

### 38
Like 8/13 with sqrt; can set sqrt coefficient 0 and use \(A^{c5}\) for \(A^{1/3}\), and \(A e^{c3 t}\) for the exponential term, kill extra linear terms. ✅ matches.

### 39
Has \(A^{c5}c6\cos(c7 t)\): to be a pure \(A^{1/3}\) term, need \(\cos(c7 t)\equiv 1\Rightarrow c7=0\). Then it’s fine; also has \(+c9\sqrt{A^2}=c9|A|\) which must be 0 to avoid extra linear term. Then reduces to matchable form. ✅ matches.

### 40
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), \(A e^{c3 t}\), and \(A^{c4} e^{c6 t}\) plus constant. To get \(A^{1/3}\) without \(t\), set \(c6=0\) and \(c4=1/3\). Kill plain \(A\) and constant by setting \(c1=0,c7=0\). ✅ matches.

### 41
Has extra \(c9\sqrt{A^2}=c9|A|\) which must be 0; then similar to 40 and can match. ✅ matches.

### 42
All terms divided by \((A^{1/3}c1+1)\). To match GT (which has no such denominator), need denominator constant 1 ⇒ \(c1=0\). Then expression becomes a linear combination of \(A^{7/3},A^{4/3}e^{c3 t},A^{1/3},A^2,A e^{c3 t},\) constants. We can zero unwanted terms and keep \(A^2\), \(A^{1/3}\), and \(A e^{c3 t}\). ✅ matches.

### 43
Similarly has denominator \((c1|A|^{1/3}+1)\); set \(c1=0\). Then you can keep \(A^2\) (via \(A^2 c0\)), keep \(A e^{c4 t}\) (via \(A c5 e^{c4 t}\)), and keep \(A^{1/3}\) (via \(c6|A|^{1/3}\)), while zeroing others. With \(A\ge0\), ✅ matches.

### 44
Has \(A^2\), \(A\), sqrt-exp, constant, and \(e^{c7|A|}|A|^{1/3}\) which is not a pure power unless \(c6=0\) (kills it) or \(c7=0\) (makes it just \(|A|^{1/3}\)). If set \(c7=0\), it becomes \(c6|A|^{1/3}\) which is fine. Then set \(A\) term 0, constant 0, set sqrt shift 0 and \(A\ge0\). ✅ matches.

### 45
Denominator \((c1|A|^{1/3}+1)\); set \(c1=0\). Then contains \(A^2\), \(A^{1/3}\), sqrt-exp times \(A^{1/3}\), sqrt-exp alone, constants. But GT needs sqrt-exp to yield \(A e^{kt}\), not \(A^{1/3}e^{kt}\). You can use the sqrt-exp-alone term \(c8\sqrt{A^2+c5}e^{c6 t}\) with \(c5=0\), \(A\ge0\) to get \(A e^{kt}\), and use \(c3|A|^{1/3}\) for the fractional term, and \(A^2 c0\) for quadratic; zero the sqrt-exp*\(A^{1/3}\) term by \(c4=0\). ✅ matches.

### 46
Has \(A^{c2}c3\cos(Ac4)\): to be pure \(A^{1/3}\), need \(\cos(Ac4)\equiv 1\Rightarrow c4=0\), and set \(c2=1/3\). Use sqrt-exp with shift 0 and \(A\ge0\) for \(A e^{kt}\). Kill constant \(c8=0\) and linear \(A\) term \(c1=0\). ✅ matches.

### 47
Has an extra \(\sin(c7 t+c8)|A|^{c9}\) term; must be removed by setting \(c6=0\). Then it reduces to 7/12-like and can match. ✅ matches.

### 48
Has a saturating term \(A^{c5}c6/(A^{c5}+c7)\) which cannot become a monomial for all \(A\) unless \(c6=0\) (kill it). Then it reduces to 13-like with \(A^2\), \(A e^{c3 t}\), \(A\) terms, constant, and \(\sqrt{A^2}\). But then no \(A^{1/3}\) term remains. ❌ no match.

### 49
Has extra \(e^{c7|A|^{c8}}\) term; can kill it by \(c6=0\). Then reduces to 7/12-like and can match. ✅ matches.

### 50
Has a saturating rational \(|A|^{c6}/(c7+|A|^{c6})\); must be killed by \(c5=0\). Then remaining terms are \(A^2\), \(A\), \(A e^{c3 t}\), constant—no \(A^{1/3}\). ❌ no match.

### 51
Has saturating rational term; can kill it by \(c2=0\). Then remaining terms are \(A^2\), \(A\), sqrt-exp, constant—no \(A^{1/3}\). ❌ no match.
